\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
This is the \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField}{Force\+Field}} class which contains all the force-\/field releated parameters, such as bond-\/lengths, angles, dihedrals, etc. It also contains the atom-\/type definition rules, and user-\/defined categories.~\newline
 This class provides all the functions to quickly access this data by storing it in an organized format.~\newline
 Various forcefields can be loaded into De\+Novo if required parameters are available. Special cases where this is not true include the \char`\"{}empty\char`\"{} forcefield and the \mbox{\hyperlink{classIncompleteForceField}{Incomplete\+Force\+Field}}~\newline
 ~\newline
See the documentation PDF for details about various forcefield parameters and the way they are stored and loaded, and the different forcefields like the \char`\"{}empty\char`\"{} forcefield and the \char`\"{}\+CHARMM-\/27\char`\"{} forcefield 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield_8hpp_source_l00317}{317}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield_8hpp_source}{forcefield.\+hpp}}.

Blank constructor for \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField}{Force\+Field}} (does not load any force-\/field parameters) 

An empty constructor which loads no parameters except default values for standard elements (such as 4 for carbon, 3 for nitrogen, etc.). It is to be called by subclass which loads the actual atom-\/types (such as \mbox{\hyperlink{classIncompleteForceField}{Incomplete\+Force\+Field}}). Ensure that any class that is derived from \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField}{Force\+Field}} and uses this constructor defines the atom-\/types (with proper force-\/field energy parameters -\/ σ,ε,q)

\index{ForceField@{ForceField}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ForceField()}{ForceField()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/5]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Force\+Field\+::\+Force\+Field (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const std\+::string \&}]{ff\+\_\+file }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Load the forcefield from the standard ffin format (see PDF documentation for format details) 

This function completely loads {\bfseries{all the required}} parameters for the atom-\/types by reading data from the file. If this wasn\textquotesingle{}t your requirement, or if data is not available, check the \mbox{\hyperlink{classIncompleteForceField}{Incomplete\+Force\+Field}} class.~\newline
 This function uses the \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField_ad172233c0a72e65847a7c91145bb9ab9}{Force\+Field\+::load\+Additional\+Atom\+Types()}} functionality.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily Force\+Field\+::\+Force\+Field (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Blank constructor for \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField}{Force\+Field}} (does not load any force-\/field parameters) 

An empty constructor which loads no parameters except default values for standard elements (such as 4 for carbon, 3 for nitrogen, etc.). It is to be called by subclass which loads the actual atom-\/types (such as \mbox{\hyperlink{classIncompleteForceField}{Incomplete\+Force\+Field}}). Ensure that any class that is derived from \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField}{Force\+Field}} and uses this constructor defines the atom-\/types (with proper force-\/field energy parameters -\/ σ,ε,q)

{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool Force\+Field\+::accept\+New\+Bond (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{src,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$ $>$}]{bnd,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{n }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Checks whether accepting a particular atom to bond to a source atom is allowed accornding to atom-\/type definitions. 

This function is similar to select\+Atom\+By\+Rule(), except instead of providing the atom to be chosen, it checks if the chosen atom satisfies the required definitions.~\newline
 It is used when checking for cyclization

\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em n} & The new atom being trialled for bonding to src \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{ForceField@{ForceField}!acceptNewBond@{acceptNewBond}}
\index{acceptNewBond@{acceptNewBond}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{acceptNewBond()}{acceptNewBond()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [4/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily bool Force\+Field\+::accept\+New\+Bond (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{src,  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$ $>$}]{bnd,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{n }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Checks whether accepting a particular atom to bond to a source atom is allowed accornding to atom-\/type definitions. 

This function is similar to select\+Atom\+By\+Rule(), except instead of providing the atom to be chosen, it checks if the chosen atom satisfies the required definitions.~\newline
 It is used when checking for cyclization 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em src} & The source atom on which the check must be performed \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em bnd} & The list of all atoms already bonded to src \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em n} & The new atom being trialled for bonding to src \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily double Force\+Field\+::calculate\+Angle\+Energy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a0,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a2,  }\item[{bool}]{rigid = {\ttfamily false},  }\item[{double}]{acut = {\ttfamily THETACUT} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Calculate the angle-\/strain potential energy (see documentation in PDF for the exact function) 

Calculates the net energy from angle parameters (including Urey-\/\+Bradley contribution -\/ See PDF)~\newline
This method can also be used as a boolean tolerance (with the help of the \char`\"{}rigid\char`\"{} flag) 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em rigid} & A boolean flag. If set to true, instead of calculating the energy, the function checks if the angle value falls within a tolerance limit (acut) of the expected value. If yes, the energy is taken to be zero, otherwise it\textquotesingle{}s ∞ \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em acut} & The angle tolerance value. The default tolerance is THETACUT \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily double Force\+Field\+::calculate\+Angle\+Energy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a0,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a2,  }\item[{bool}]{rigid = {\ttfamily false},  }\item[{double}]{acut = {\ttfamily THETACUT} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Calculate the angle-\/strain potential energy (see documentation in PDF for the exact function) 

Calculates the net energy from angle parameters (including Urey-\/\+Bradley contribution -\/ See PDF)~\newline
This method can also be used as a boolean tolerance (with the help of the \char`\"{}rigid\char`\"{} flag) 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em rigid} & A boolean flag. If set to true, instead of calculating the energy, the function checks if the angle value falls within a tolerance limit (acut) of the expected value. If yes, the energy is taken to be zero, otherwise it\textquotesingle{}s ∞ \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em acut} & The angle tolerance value. The default tolerance is THETACUT \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

Note that this is different from select\+Atom\+By\+Rule() which considers the atoms bonded to the source atom.~\newline
This function only provides a list of all possible bonds that this atom-\/type can have

\index{getAngleParamtersFailsafe@{getAngleParamtersFailsafe}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getAngleParamtersFailsafe()}{getAngleParamtersFailsafe()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [4/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const std\+::vector$<$ double $>$ \& Force\+Field\+::get\+Angle\+Paramters\+Failsafe (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a2,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a3 }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Get the bond angle for the angle between three atom types. -\/failsafe method. 

Searches the angle data loaded into this force-\/field to find angle parameters for a given triplet of atom types. It also checks if any templates match the request (see input files section of documentation PDF)~\newline
 If it is not found, it will print a warning message (stating that data could not be found), and will resort to a default value (instead of throwing an exception -\/ which is why this method has \char`\"{}failsafe\char`\"{} in the name). 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield__precomp__omega__stable2_8hpp_source_l00791}{791}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield__precomp__omega__stable2_8hpp_source}{forcefield\+\_\+precomp\+\_\+omega\+\_\+stable2.\+hpp}}.

Searches the dihedral data for a {\bfseries{direct match}} only (no template matching). If dihedral data is not found, \mbox{\hyperlink{classDataNotAvailableException}{Data\+Not\+Available\+Exception}} is thrown.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getDihedralParametersFailsafe()}{getDihedralParametersFailsafe()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily const std\+::vector$<$ double $>$ \& Force\+Field\+::get\+Dihedral\+Parameters\+Failsafe (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a1,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a2,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a3,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a4 }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Get the dihedral angle for a set of four atoms (in order of the chain). -\/failsafe method. 

Searches the dihedral data loaded into this force-\/field to find dihedral parameters for a given set of atom types. It also checks if any templates match the request (see input files section of documentation PDF)~\newline
 If it is not found, it will print a warning message (stating that data could not be found), and will resort to a default value (instead of throwing an exception -\/ which is why this method has \char`\"{}failsafe\char`\"{} in the name). 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield_8hpp_source_l00926}{926}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield_8hpp_source}{forcefield.\+hpp}}.

Get the list of all the rules loaded into this forcefield.

Get a list of the loaded atom-\/types such that they can bond to the source atom (see params).~\newline
 This function ensures that after adding this bond, the no atom-\/type definitions are violated. No checks are made to ensure that all the rules can still be satisfied after this stage. It is assumed that the rules are sane enough to allow the atom-\/type to satisfy them

Situationally list atoms that can bond to the selected atom. 

Get a list of the loaded atom-\/types such that they can bond to the source atom (see params).~\newline
 This function ensures that after adding this bond, the no atom-\/type definitions are violated. No checks are made to ensure that all the rules can still be satisfied after this stage. It is assumed that the rules are sane enough to allow the atom-\/type to satisfy them \mbox{\Hypertarget{classForceField_a916b6f2de77e5c712e9e3404d7862a1a}\label{classForceField_a916b6f2de77e5c712e9e3404d7862a1a}}

\index{loadBondParameters@{loadBondParameters}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{loadBondParameters()}{loadBondParameters()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void Force\+Field\+::load\+Bond\+Parameters (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::string}]{lengthfn = {\ttfamily LengthDataFile},  }\item[{std\+::string}]{anglefn = {\ttfamily AngleDataFile},  }\item[{std\+::string}]{dihedralfn = {\ttfamily DihedralDataFile},  }\item[{std\+::string}]{improperfn = {\ttfamily ImproperDataFile},  }\item[{bool}]{erase = {\ttfamily true} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



A wrapper to load all parameters (bond-\/length,bond-\/angle,dihedral,and improper-\/dihedral). See documentation (PDF) for default filenames. 

This function is a wrapper to load all required parameters at once using default (or, based on programmer\textquotesingle{}s choice, other specified) input files for the data.~\newline
 To load any of bond length, angle, dihedral, or improper parameters separately, look at the respective functions (\mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField_a00fd23cd72bc2fb9037b744befae5180}{Force\+Field\+::load\+Lengths}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField_a4e91de8d02133714b409ad4374346314}{Force\+Field\+::load\+Angles}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField_a2247bad6012ae2d0897abb532a072d47}{Force\+Field\+::load\+Dihedrals}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{classForceField_a4871a728498d1cd28e5cfc2130b99a53}{Force\+Field\+::load\+Impropers}}). 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em lengthfn} & Filename to load \uline{length} data (1st parameter) \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em anglefn} & Filename to load \uline{angle} data (2nd parameter) \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em dihedralfn} & Filename to load \uline{{\bfseries{proper}} dihedral} data (3rd parameter) \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em improperfn} & Filename to load \uline{{\bfseries{improper}} dihedral} data (4th parameter) \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em erase} & Delete any pre-\/existing data? (Default\+: Yes) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\index{ForceField@{ForceField}!loadImpropers@{loadImpropers}}
\index{loadImpropers@{loadImpropers}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{loadImpropers()}{loadImpropers()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void Force\+Field\+::load\+Impropers (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const std\+::string \&}]{s }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Load improper dihedral data from a given file (not used in later versions of De\+Novo) 

De\+Novo Versions after SIGMA do not deal with improper dihedrals except for fallback cases or for programming explicit requirements.~\newline
 The data for those parameters has not been updated since, and many new atom types (and parameters for existing atom-\/types) have been added for all other bonding data, so be sure to check the data for completeness and validity before using this feature.~\newline
 {\bfseries{Warning\+: }} For all practical purposes and general use of the De\+Novo, this feature is considered {\itshape deprecated}.

\index{ForceField@{ForceField}!loadResidues@{loadResidues}}
\index{loadResidues@{loadResidues}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{loadResidues()}{loadResidues()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void Force\+Field\+::load\+Residues (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const std\+::string \&}]{resf }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Load residues from an RTP file. 

Standard RTP files can be used by De\+Novo for loading residues. Each residue has unique atom names for each atom which is then mapped to a forcefield atom type. (Open protein.\+rtp attached with De\+Novo to see the format)~\newline
 These files can be found in GROMACS data files, or (with enough effort) written manually. It\textquotesingle{}s preferred to use GROMACS rtp files so that GROMACS can be used to convert/rewrite PDB files (and hence the atom-\/type names and unique names of all the atoms match)~\newline
 The protein.\+rtp and dna.\+rtp files are taken from GROMACS data files for the CHARMM-\/27 forcefield based on which the De\+Novo generation is based as well. 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield_8hpp_source_l01183}{1183}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{forcefield_8hpp_source}{forcefield.\+hpp}}.

Load rules from a given file. 

Rules define what atom-\/atom bonds are allowed, and how many. See the atom-\/type definition section of documentation PDF for more details on format.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{classForceField_a314a55483177e20397b04e185b37b2ed}\label{classForceField_a314a55483177e20397b04e185b37b2ed}} 
\index{ForceField@{ForceField}!selectAtomByRule@{selectAtomByRule}}
\index{selectAtomByRule@{selectAtomByRule}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{selectAtomByRule()}{selectAtomByRule()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$ Force\+Field\+::select\+Atom\+By\+Rule (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{s,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classMolecule}{Molecule}} $\ast$}]{m,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{temp = {\ttfamily nullptr} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Situationally choose an atom that can bond to the selected atom. 

Get a copy of one of the loaded atom-\/types such that it can bond to the source atom (see params).~\newline
 This function ensures that after adding this bond, the no atom-\/type definitions are violated. No checks are made to ensure that all the rules can still be satisfied after this stage. It is assumed that the rules are sane enough to allow the atom-\/type to satisfy them \mbox{\Hypertarget{classForceField_a95d0676e821612c47f3675c790cac28a}\label{classForceField_a95d0676e821612c47f3675c790cac28a}} 
\index{ForceField@{ForceField}!selectRandomBondableAtom@{selectRandomBondableAtom}}
\index{selectRandomBondableAtom@{selectRandomBondableAtom}!ForceField@{ForceField}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{selectRandomBondableAtom()}{selectRandomBondableAtom()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$ Force\+Field\+::select\+Random\+Bondable\+Atom (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{bias = {\ttfamily nullptr} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Get a random atom that can bond to this atom but bias the output. 

This function biases the output of the random result to return an atom-\/type of the same element as the biasing atom (actually it biases using the first character, so CL and BR cannot be bias targets)~\newline
 If no such atom-\/type is available, then a random atom is returned. If multiple atom-\/types of the bias element are available, one is chosen randomly. 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em a} & The atom which has to form the bond \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em bias} & The atom-\/type (technically element) to which to bias the result \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{selectRandomBondableAtomTerminal()}{selectRandomBondableAtomTerminal()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$ Force\+Field\+::select\+Random\+Bondable\+Atom\+Terminal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{a,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classAtom}{Atom}} $\ast$}]{bias = {\ttfamily nullptr} }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Get a random terminal atom that can bond to this atom but bias the output. 

This function biases the output of the random result to return an atom-\/type of the same element as the biasing atom (actually it biases using the first character, so CL and BR cannot be bias targets)~\newline
If no such atom-\/type is available, then a random atom is returned. If multiple atom-\/types of the bias element are available, one is chosen randomly.~\newline
 Note that this function specifically looks for a {\bfseries{terminal}} atom. If no terminals are possible, a nullptr is returned. 
\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em a} & The atom which has to form the bond \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em bias} & The atom-\/type (technically element) to which to bias the result \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
